<Review>The Salty Bear brewing company is a brand new brewery to me! I didn't even know they were around until my friend posted a pint of beer with a logo I didn't recognize.  They're located on the same street as Gunwhale ales and Barley Forge.  Leaning more along the lines of ales.

The atmosphere is chill with an island vibe music (Friday about 7pm).  Place was packed with patrons inside and outside on the patio outside.

Beers are mainly ales, but also vary from Gose's to I've seen one porter so far.  I tend to lean towards the stronger ABV and Belgian Styles and Salty Bear has a great Belgian strong ale.

Unfortunately there is no food cooked here, but fortunately food can be brought in or ordered since they are right behind the CAMP, Costa Mesa.

Check this place out!<//Review>< pics>

<Text>If you don't care about your pet, you can have 'em put down here.

No moping in this place - the vet walked in only 25 minutes late for our scheduled meeting, and didn't waste time with boring explanations or apologies - there are things to be done in a day, after all. She must have known that we'd paid in advance, and decided that speed was the order of the day.

She got right into Super Customer Service Mode, gave us a cheery a smile and asked in a bright voice "So! What are we doing?" and I have to be impressed with the sheer concentration manifested to blithely ignore not only the schedule, but also that room: two solemn-faced individuals gently cradling an old, blind chihuahua with tears on their faces isn't an easy thing to power through, but she managed it without batting an eye - didn't even phase her - that's experience, there.

This human female didn't mince around with the needle, either. I mean, some vets get so dainty when dealing with a small dog that the injection takes a full twenty or thirty seconds - she apparently had no time for that (I mean, she was obviously running at least 25 minutes behind schedule; we knew this was a busy day from 'go'.).

I reckon she doesn't see the point in sparing the injection on an animal that's going to die in a few minutes anyway, when there are other things to be done! So she really just jabbed it into the butt muscle and immediately plunged the syringe down - must have taken three seconds tops, during which this slow, tired dog whipped around and flailed in pain. Hadn't seen her move that fast in over a year.

She wanders back in fifteen minutes later with someone else, a bit more of a touchy-feely woman who obviously cares about animals. Don't you just hate it when you have to change gears because someone is watching? Only took three tries to find a vein for the lethal injection, and she announced death only a little prematurely - but it's not like this is an exact science or anything.

Yes, my tone is caustic and my review is laced with sarcasm. I'm too pissed to write it any other way just now, so I'll end it with this: if you want to see a friend die in needless pain at the hands of an unprofessional disrespectful woman of questionable ability and apparently no compassion who doesn't arrive on time... < Review>
I was a little apprehensive at first and I asked a LOT of questions about the 2013 Mazda 3 before I bought it.

I noticed that the driver seat belt was pretty messed up and the back tires were cupping pretty bad. I told my sales associate Bill about it and they hooked it up with 4 brand new tires and an OEM Mazda Seat Belt.

I also checked and the fluids were all topped off and the oil's consistency looked like it just had a fresh oil change. I would recommend checking these things before buying any used car.

They tried hard to get me into a car right away and they were able to get me a loan with a really decent APR even though I had a bankruptcy and repo on my record.

If your credit is in bad shape, I would recommend coming to these guys. They'll do everything they can to get you into a car that you want. If you find any issues with the vehicle just tell them about it and they'd more than happy to help.</Review>
